}\\n213: \\n214:     private void addToInflightBatches(List<ProducerBatch> batches) {\\n215:         for (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\\n216:             List<ProducerBatch> inflightBatchList = inFlightBatches.computeIfAbsent(batch.topicPartition,\\n217:                 k -> new ArrayList<>());\\n218:             inflightBatchList.add(batch);\\n219:         }\\n220:     }\\n221: \\n222: addToInflightBatches(batchList);\\n225:         }\\n226:     }\\n227: \\n228:     private boolean hasPendingTransactionalRequests() {\\n229:         return transactionManager != null && transactionManager.hasPendingRequests() && transactionManager.hasOngoingTransaction();\\n230:     }\\n231: \\n232:     /**\\n233:      * The main run loop for the sender thread\\n234:      */\\n235:     @Override\\n236:     public void run() {\\n237:         log.debug(\\\"Starting Kafka producer I/O thread.\\\");\\n238: \\n239:         // main loop, runs until close is called\\n240:         while (running) {\\n241:             try {\\n242:                 runOnce();\\n243:             } catch (Exception e) {\\n244:                 log.error(\\\"Uncaught error in kafka producer I/O thread: \\\", e);\\n245:             }\\n246:         }\\n247: \\n248:         log.debug(\\\"Beginning shutdown of Kafka producer I/O thread, sending remaining records.\\\");\\n249: \\n250:         // okay we stopped accepting requests but there may still be\\n251:         // requests in the transaction manager, accumulator or waiting for acknowledgment,\\n252:         // wait until these are completed.\\n253:         while (!forceClose && ((this.accumulator.hasUndrained() || this.client.inFlightRequestCount() > 0) || hasPendingTransactionalRequests())) {\\n254:             try {\\n255:                 runOnce();\\n256:             } catch (Exception e) {\\n257:                 log.error(\\\"Uncaught error in kafka producer I/O thread: \\\", e);\\n258:             }\\n259:         }\\n260: \\n261:         // Abort the transaction if any commit or abort didn't go through the transaction manager's queue\\n262:         while (!forceClose && transactionManager != null && transactionManager.hasOngoingTransaction()) {\\n263:             if (!transactionManager.isCompleting()) {\\n264:                 log.info(\\\"Aborting incomplete transaction due to shutdown\\\");\\n265:                 try {\\n266:                     // It is possible for the transaction manager to throw errors when aborting. Catch these\\n267:                     // so as not to interfere with the rest of the shutdown logic.\\n268:                     transactionManager.beginAbort();\\n269:                 } catch (Exception e) {\\n270:                     log.error(\\\"Error in kafka producer I/O thread while aborting transaction when during closing: \\\", e);\\n271:                     // Force close in case the transactionManager is in error states.\\n272:                     forceClose = true;\\n273:                 }\\n274:             }\\n275:             try {\\n276:                 runOnce();\\n277:             } catch (Exception e) {\\n278:                 log.error(\\\"Uncaught error in kafka producer I/O thread: \\\", e);\\n279:             }\\n280:         }\\n281: \\n282:         if (forceClose) {\\n283:             // We need to fail all the incomplete transactional requests and batches and wake up the threads waiting on\\n284:             // the futures.\\n285:             if (transactionManager != null) {\\n286:                 log.debug(\\\"Aborting incomplete transactional requests due to forced shutdown\\\");\\n287:                 transactionManager.close();\\n288:             }\\n289:             log.debug(\\\"Aborting incomplete batches due to forced shutdown\\\");\\n290:             this.accumulator.abortIncompleteBatches();\\n291:         }\\n292:         try {\\n293:             this.client.close();\\n294:         } catch (Exception e) {\\n295:             log.error(\\\"Failed to close network client\\\", e);\\n296:         }\\n297: \\n298:         log.debug(\\\"Shutdown of Kafka producer I/O thread has completed.\\\");\\n299:     }\\n300: \\n301:     /**\\n302:      * Run a single iteration of sending\\n303:      *\\n304:      */\\n305:     void runOnce() {\\n306:         if (transactionManager != null) {\\n307:             try {\\n308:                 transactionManager.maybeResolveSequences();\\n309: \\n310:                 RuntimeException lastError = transactionManager.lastError();\\n311: \\n312:                 // do not continue sending if the transaction manager is in a failed state\\n313:                 if (transactionManager.hasFatalError()) {\\n314:                     if (lastError != null)\\n315:                         maybeAbortBatches(lastError);\\n316:                     client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\\n317:                     return;\\n318:                 }\\n319: \\n320:                 if (transactionManager.hasAbortableError() && shouldHandleAuthorizationError(lastError)) {\\n321:                     return;\\n322:                 }\\n323: \\n324:                 // Check whether we need a new producerId. If so, we will enqueue an InitProducerId\\n325:                 // request which will be sent below\\n326:                 transactionManager.bumpIdempotentEpochAndResetIdIfNeeded();\\n327: \\n328:                 if (maybeSendAndPollTransactionalRequest()) {\\n329:                     return;\\n330:                 }\\n331:             } catch (AuthenticationException e) {\\n332:                 // This is already logged as error, but propagated here to perform any clean ups.\\n333:                 log.trace(\\\"Authentication exception while processing transactional request\\\", e);\\n334:                 transactionManager.authenticationFailed(e);\\n335:             }\\n336:         }\\n337: \\n338:         long currentTimeMs = time.milliseconds();\\n339:         long pollTimeout = sendProducerData(currentTimeMs);\\n340:         client.poll(pollTimeout, currentTimeMs);\\n341:     }\\n342: \\n343:     // We handle {@code TransactionalIdAuthorizationException} and {@code ClusterAuthorizationException} by first\\n344:     // failing the inflight requests, then transition the state to UNINITIALIZED so that the user doesn't need to\\n345:     // instantiate the producer again.\\n346:     private boolean shouldHandleAuthorizationError(RuntimeException exception) {\\n347:         if (exception instanceof TransactionalIdAuthorizationException ||\\n348:                         exception instanceof ClusterAuthorizationException) {\\n349:             transactionManager.failPendingRequests(new AuthenticationException(exception));\\n350:             maybeAbortBatches(exception);\\n351:             transactionManager.transitionToUninitialized(exception);\\n352:             return true;\\n353:         }\\n354:         return false;\\n355:     }\\n356: \\n357:     private long sendProducerData(long now) {\\n358:         MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot = metadata.fetchMetadataSnapshot();\\n359:         // get the list of partitions with data ready to send\\n360:         RecordAccumulator.ReadyCheckResult result = this.accumulator.ready(metadataSnapshot, now);\\n361: \\n362:         // if there are any partitions whose leaders are not known yet, force metadata update\\n363:         if (!result.unknownLeaderTopics.isEmpty()) {\\n364:             // The set of topics with unknown leader contains topics with leader election pending as well as\\n365:             // topics which may have expired. Add the topic again to metadata to ensure it is included\\n366:             // and request metadata update, since there are messages to send to the topic.\\n367:             for (String topic : result.unknownLeaderTopics)\\n368:                 this.metadata.add(topic, now);\\n369: \\n370:             log.debug(\\\"Requesting metadata update due to unknown leader topics from the batched records: {}\\\",\\n371:                 result.unknownLeaderTopics);\\n372:             this.metadata.requestUpdate(false);\\n373:         }\\n374: \\n375:         // remove any nodes we aren't ready to send to\\n376:         Iterator<Node> iter = result.readyNodes.iterator();\\n377:         long notReadyTimeout = Long.MAX_VALUE;\\n378:         while (iter.hasNext()) {\\n379:             Node node = iter.next();\\n380:             if (!this.client.ready(node, now)) {\\n381:                 // Update just the readyTimeMs of the latency stats, so that it moves forward\\n382:                 // every time the batch is ready (then the difference between readyTimeMs and\\n383:                 // drainTimeMs would represent how long data is waiting for the node).\\n384:                 this.accumulator.updateNodeLatencyStats(node.id(), now, false);\\n385:                 iter.remove();\\n386:                 notReadyTimeout = Math.min(notReadyTimeout, this.client.pollDelayMs(node, now));\\n387:             } else {\\n388:                 // Update both readyTimeMs and drainTimeMs, this would \\\"reset\\\" the node\\n389:                 // latency.\\n390:                 this.accumulator.updateNodeLatencyStats(node.id(), now, true);\\n391:             }\\n392:         }\\n393: \\n394:         // create produce requests\\n395:         Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(metadataSnapshot, result.readyNodes, this.maxRequestSize, now);\\n396:         addToInflightBatches(batches);\\n397:         if (guaranteeMessageOrder) {\\n398:             // Mute all the partitions drained\\n399:             for (List<ProducerBatch> batchList : batches.values()) {\\n400:                 for (ProducerBatch batch : batchList)\\n401:                     this.accumulator.mutePartition(batch.topicPartition);\\n402:             }\\n403:         }\\n404: \\n405:         accumulator.resetNextBatchExpiryTime();\\n406:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\\n409: \\n410:         // Reset the producer id if an expired batch has previously been sent to the broker. Also update the metrics\\n411:         // for expired batches. see the documentation of @TransactionState.resetIdempotentProducerId to understand why\\n412:         // we need to reset the producer id here.\\n413:         if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty())\\n414:             log.trace(\\\"Expired {} batches in accumulator\\\", expiredBatches.size());\\n415:         for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\\n416:             String errorMessage = \\\"Expiring \\\" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \\\" record(s) for \\\" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\\n417:                 + \\\":\\\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \\\" ms has passed since batch creation\\\";\\n418:             failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\\n419:             if (transactionManager != null && expiredBatch.inRetry()) {\\n420:                 // This ensures that no new batches are drained until the current in flight batches are fully resolved.\\n421:                 transactionManager.markSequenceUnresolved(expiredBatch);\\n422:             }\\n423:         }\\n424:         sensors.updateProduceRequestMetrics(batches);\\n425: \\n426:         // If we have any nodes that are ready to send + have sendable data, poll with 0 timeout so this can immediately\\n427:         // loop and try sending more data. Otherwise, the timeout will be the smaller value between next batch expiry\\n428:         // time, and the delay time for checking data availability. Note that the nodes may have data that isn't yet\\n429:         // sendable due to lingering, backing off, etc. This specifically does not include nodes with sendable data\\n430:         // that aren't ready to send since they would cause busy looping.\\n431:         long pollTimeout = Math.min(result.nextReadyCheckDelayMs, notReadyTimeout);\\n432:         pollTimeout = Math.min(pollTimeout, this.accumulator.nextExpiryTimeMs() - now);\\n433:         pollTimeout = Math.max(pollTimeout, 0);\\n434:         if (!result.readyNodes.isEmpty()) {\\n435:             log.trace(\\\"Nodes with data ready to send: {}\\\", result.readyNodes);\\n436:             // if some partitions are already ready to be sent, the select time would be 0;\\n437:             // otherwise if some partition already has some data accumulated but not ready yet,\\n438:             // the select time will be the time difference between now and its linger expiry time;\\n439:             // otherwise the select time will be the time difference between now and the metadata expiry time;\\n440:             pollTimeout = 0;\\n441:         }\\n442:         sendProduceRequests(batches, now);\\n443:         return pollTimeout;\\n444:     }\\n445: \\n446:     /**\\n447:      * Returns true if a transactional request is sent or polled, or if a FindCoordinator request is enqueued\\n448:      */\\n449:     private boolean maybeSendAndPollTransactionalRequest() {\\n450:         if (transactionManager.hasInFlightRequest()) {\\n451:             // as long as there are outstanding transactional requests, we simply wait for them to return\\n452:             client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\\n453:             return true;\\n454:         }\\n455: \\n456:         if (transactionManager.hasAbortableError()) {\\n457:             accumulator.abortUndrainedBatches(transactionManager.lastError());\\n458:         } else if (transactionManager.isAborting()) {\\n459:             accumulator.abortUndrainedBatches(new TransactionAbortedException());\\n460:         }\\n461: \\n462:         TransactionManager.TxnRequestHandler nextRequestHandler = transactionManager.nextRequest(accumulator.hasIncomplete());\\n463:         if (nextRequestHandler == null)\\n464:             return false;\\n465: \\n466:         AbstractRequest.Builder<?> nextRequestHandler.coordinatorType();\\n470:             targetNode = coordinatorType != null ?\\n471:                     transactionManager.coordinator(coordinatorType) :\\n472: finding coordinator.\\\", coordinatorType, requestBuilder.apiKey());\\n481:                 maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(nextRequestHandler);\\n482:                 return true;\\n483:             } else {\\n484:                 log.trace(\\\"No nodes available to send requests, will poll and retry when until a node is ready.\\\");\\n485:                 transactionManager.retry(nextRequestHandler);\\n486:                 client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\\n487:                 return true;\\n488:             }\\n489: \\n490:             if (nextRequestHandler.isRetry())\\n491:                 time.sleep(nextRequestHandler.retryBackoffMs());\\n492: \\n493:             long currentTimeMs = time.milliseconds();\\n494:             ClientRequest clientRequest = client.newClientRequest(targetNode.idString(), requestBuilder, currentTimeMs,\\n495:                 true, requestTimeoutMs, nextRequestHandler);\\n496:             log.debug(\\\"Sending transactional request {} to node {} with correlation ID {}\\\", requestBuilder, targetNode, clientRequest.correlationId());\\n497:             client.send(clientRequest, currentTimeMs);\\n498:             transactionManager.setInFlightCorrelationId(clientRequest.correlationId());\\n499:             client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\\n500: Going \\\" +\\n503:                     \\\"to back off and retry.\\\", targetNode, requestBuilder, e);\\n504:             // We break here so that we pick up the FindCoordinator request immediately.\\n505:             maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(nextRequestHandler);\\n506:             return true;\\n507:         }\\n508:     }\\n509: \\n510:     private void maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(TransactionManager.TxnRequestHandler nextRequestHandler) {\\n511:         if (nextRequestHandler.needsCoordinator()) {\\n512:             transactionManager.lookupCoordinator(nextRequestHandler);\\n513:         } else {\\n514:             // For non-coordinator requests, sleep here to prevent a tight loop when no node is available\\n515:             time.sleep(retryBackoffMs);\\n516:             metadata.requestUpdate(false);\\n517:         }\\n518: \\n519:         transactionManager.retry(nextRequestHandler);\\n520:     }\\n521: \\n522:     private void maybeAbortBatches(RuntimeException exception) {\\n523:         if (accumulator.hasIncomplete()) {\\n524:             log.error(\\\"Aborting producer batches due to fatal error\\\", exception);\\n525:             accumulator.abortBatches(exception);\\n526:         }\\n527:     }\\n528: \\n529:     /**\\n530:      * Start closing the sender (won't actually complete until all data is sent out)\\n531:      */\\n532:     public void initiateClose() {\\n533:         // Ensure accumulator is closed first to guarantee that no more appends are accepted after\\n534:         // breaking from the sender loop. Otherwise, we may miss some callbacks when shutting down.\\n535:         this.accumulator.close();\\n536:         this.running = false;\\n537:         this.wakeup();\\n538:     }\\n539: \\n540:     /**\\n541:      * Closes the sender without sending out any pending messages.\\n542:      */\\n543:     public void forceClose() {\\n544:         this.forceClose = true;\\n545: FindCoordinatorRequest.CoordinatorType coordinatorType) throws IOException {\\n553:         if (NetworkClientUtils.awaitReady(client, node, time, requestTimeoutMs)) {\\n554:             if (coordinatorType == FindCoordinatorRequest.CoordinatorType.TRANSACTION) {\\n555:                 // Indicate to the transaction manager that the coordinator is ready, allowing it to check ApiVersions\\n556:                 // This allows us to bump transactional epochs even if the coordinator is temporarily unavailable at\\n557:                 // the time when the abortable error is \\n565:     /**\\n566:      * Handle a produce response\\n567:      */\\n568:     private void handleProduceResponse(ClientResponse response, Map<TopicPartition, ProducerBatch> batches, Map<Uuid, String> topicNames, long now) {\\n569:         RequestHeader requestHeader = response.requestHeader();\\n570:         int correlationId = requestHeader.correlationId();\\n571:         if (response.wasTimedOut()) {\\n572:             log.trace(\\\"Cancelled request with header {} due to the last request to node {} timed out\\\",\\n573:                 requestHeader, response.destination());\\n574:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\\n575:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.REQUEST_TIMED_OUT, String.format(\\\"Disconnected from node %s due to timeout\\\", response.destination())),\\n576:                         correlationId, now, null);\\n577:         } else if (response.wasDisconnected()) {\\n578:             log.trace(\\\"Cancelled request with header {} due to node {} being disconnected\\\",\\n579:                 requestHeader, response.destination());\\n580:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\\n581:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.NETWORK_EXCEPTION, String.format(\\\"Disconnected from node %s\\\", response.destination())),\\n582:                         correlationId, now, null);\\n583:         } else if (response.versionMismatch() != null) {\\n584:             log.warn(\\\"Cancelled request {} due to a version mismatch with node {}\\\",\\n585:                     response, response.destination(), response.versionMismatch());\\n586:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\\n587:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.UNSUPPORTED_VERSION), correlationId, now, null);\\n588:         } else {\\n589:             log.trace(\\\"Received produce response from node {} with correlation id {}\\\", response.destination(), correlationId);\\n590:             // if we have a response, parse it\\n591:             if (response.hasResponse()) {\\n592:                 // Sender should exercise PartitionProduceResponse rather than ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse\\n593:                 // https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-10696\\n594:                 ProduceResponse produceResponse = (ProduceResponse) response.responseBody();\\n595:                 // This will be set by completeBatch.\\n596:                 Map<TopicPartition, Metadata.LeaderIdAndEpoch> partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo = new HashMap<>();\\n597:                 produceResponse.data().responses().forEach(r -> r.partitionResponses().forEach(p -> {\\n598:                     ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse partResp = new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(\\n599:                             Errors.forCode(p.errorCode()),\\n600:                             p.baseOffset(),\\n601:                             p.logAppendTimeMs(),\\n602:                             p.logStartOffset(),\\n603:                             p.recordErrors()\\n604:                                 .stream()\\n605:                                 .map(e -> new ProduceResponse.RecordError(e.batchIndex(), e.batchIndexErrorMessage()))\\n606:                                 .collect(Collectors.toList()),\\n607:                             p.errorMessage(),\\n608:                             p.currentLeader());\\n609: \\n610:                     // Version 13 drop topic name and add support to topic id.\\n611:                     // We need to find batch based on topic id and partition index only as\\n612:                     // topic name in the response will be empty.\\n613:                     // For older versions, topic id is zero, and we will find the batch based on the topic name.\\n614:                     TopicPartition tp = (!r.topicId().equals(Uuid.ZERO_UUID) && topicNames.containsKey(r.topicId())) ?\\n615:                             new TopicPartition(topicNames.get(r.topicId()), p.index()) :\\n616:                             new TopicPartition(r.name(), p.index());\\n617: \\n618:                     ProducerBatch batch = batches.get(tp);\\n619:                     if (batch == null) {\\n620:                         throw new IllegalStateException(\\\"Can't find batch created for topic id \\\" + r.topicId() +\\n621:                                 \\\" topic name \\\" + r.name() + \\\" partition \\\" + p.index() + \\\" using \\\" + topicNames);\\n622:                     }\\n623:                     completeBatch(batch, partResp, correlationId, now, partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo);\\n624:                 }));\\n625: \\n626:                 if (!partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo.isEmpty()) {\\n627:                     List<Node> leaderNodes = produceResponse.data().nodeEndpoints().stream()\\n628:                         .map(e -> new Node(e.nodeId(), e.host(), e.port(), e.rack()))\\n629:                         .filter(e -> !e.equals(Node.noNode()))\\n630:                         .collect(\\n631:                             Collectors.toList());\\n632:                     Set<TopicPartition> updatedPartitions = metadata.updatePartitionLeadership(partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo, leaderNodes);\\n633:                     if (log.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n634:                         updatedPartitions.forEach(\\n635:                             part -> log.debug(\\\"For {} leader was updated.\\\", part)\\n636:                         );\\n637:                     }\\n638:                 }\\n639: \\n640:                 this.sensors.recordLatency(response.destination(), response.requestLatencyMs());\\n641:             } else {\\n642:                 // this is the acks = 0 case, just complete all requests\\n643:                 for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values()) {\\n644:                     completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.NONE), correlationId, now, null);\\n645:                 }\\n646:             }\\n647:         }\\n648:     }\\n649: \\n650:     /**\\n651:      * Complete or retry the given batch of records.\\n652:      *\\n653:      * @param batch The record batch\\n654:      * @param response The produce response\\n655:      * @param correlationId The correlation id for the request\\n656:      * @param now The current POSIX timestamp in milliseconds\\n657:      * @param partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo This will be populated with partitions that have updated leader info.\\n658:      */\\n659:     private void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response, long correlationId,\\n660:                                long now, Map<TopicPartition, Metadata.LeaderIdAndEpoch> partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo) {\\n661:         Errors error = response.error;\\n662: \\n663:         if (error == Errors.MESSAGE_TOO_LARGE && batch.recordCount > 1 && !batch.isDone() &&\\n664:                 (batch.magic() >= RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2 || batch.isCompressed())) {\\n665:             // If the batch is too large, we split the batch and send the split batches again. We do not decrement\\n666:             // the retry attempts in this case.\\n667:             log.warn(\\n668:                 \\\"Got error produce response in correlation id {} on topic-partition {}, splitting and retrying ({} attempts left). Error: {}\\\",\\n669:                 correlationId,\\n670:                 batch.topicPartition,\\n671:                 this.retries - batch.attempts(),\\n672:                 formatErrMsg(response));\\n673:             if (transactionManager != null)\\n674:                 transactionManager.removeInFlightBatch(batch);\\n675:             this.accumulator.splitAndReenqueue(batch);\\n676:             maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\\n677:             this.sensors.recordBatchSplit();\\n678:         } else if (error != Errors.NONE) {\\n679:             if (canRetry(batch, response, now)) {\\n680:                 log.warn(\\n681:                     \\\"Got error produce response with correlation id {} on topic-partition {}, retrying ({} attempts left). Error: {}\\\",\\n682:                     correlationId,\\n683:                     batch.topicPartition,\\n684:                     this.retries - batch.attempts() - 1,\\n685:                     formatErrMsg(response));\\n686:                 reenqueueBatch(batch, now);\\n687:             } else if (error == Errors.DUPLICATE_SEQUENCE_NUMBER) {\\n688:                 // If we have received a duplicate sequence error, it means that the sequence number has advanced beyond\\n689:                 // the sequence of the current batch, and we haven't retained batch metadata on the broker to return\\n690:                 // the correct offset and timestamp.\\n691:                 //\\n692:                 // The only thing we can do is to return success to the user and not return a valid offset and timestamp.\\n693:                 completeBatch(batch, response);\\n694:             } else {\\n695:                 // tell the user the result of their request. We only adjust sequence numbers if the batch didn't exhaust\\n696:                 // its retries -- if it did, we don't know whether the sequence number was accepted or not, and\\n697:                 // thus it is not safe to reassign the sequence.\\n698:                 failBatch(batch, response, batch.attempts() < this.retries);\\n699:             }\\n700:             if (error.exception() instanceof InvalidMetadataException) {\\n701:                 if (error.exception() instanceof UnknownTopicOrPartitionException) {\\n702:                     log.warn(\\\"Received unknown topic or partition error in produce request on partition {}. The \\\" +\\n703:                             \\\"topic-partition may not exist or the user may not have Describe access to it\\\",\\n704:                         batch.topicPartition);\\n705:                 } else {\\n706:                     log.warn(\\\"Received invalid metadata error in produce request on partition {} due to {} Going \\\" +\\n707:                             \\\"to request metadata update now\\\", batch.topicPartition, error.exception(response.errorMessage).toString());\\n708:                 }\\n709:                 if (error.exception() instanceof NotLeaderOrFollowerException || error.exception() instanceof FencedLeaderEpochException) {\\n710:                     log.debug(\\\"For {}, received error {}, with leaderIdAndEpoch {}\\\", batch.topicPartition, error, response.currentLeader);\\n711:                     if (partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo != null\\n712:                         && (response.currentLeader.leaderId() != -1 && response.currentLeader.leaderEpoch() != -1)) {\\n713:                         partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo.put(batch.topicPartition, new Metadata.LeaderIdAndEpoch(\\n714:                             Optional.of(response.currentLeader.leaderId()), Optional.of(response.currentLeader.leaderEpoch())));\\n715:                     }\\n716:                 }\\n717:                 metadata.requestUpdate(false);\\n718:             }\\n719:         } else {\\n720:             completeBatch(batch, response);\\n721:         }\\n722: \\n723:         // Unmute the completed partition.\\n724:         if (guaranteeMessageOrder)\\n725:             this.accumulator.unmutePartition(batch.topicPartition);\\n726:     }\\n727: \\n728:     /**\\n729:      * Format the error from a {@link ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse} in a user-friendly string\\n730:      * e.g \\\"NETWORK_EXCEPTION. Error Message: Disconnected from node 0\\\"\\n731:      */\\n732:     private String formatErrMsg(ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\\n733:         String errorMessageSuffix = (response.errorMessage == null || response.errorMessage.isEmpty()) ?\\n734:                 \\\"\\\" : String.format(\\\". Error Message: %s\\\", response.errorMessage);\\n735:         return String.format(\\\"%s%s\\\", response.error, errorMessageSuffix);\\n736:     }\\n737: \\n738:     private void reenqueueBatch(ProducerBatch batch, long currentTimeMs) {\\n739:         this.accumulator.reenqueue(batch, currentTimeMs);\\n740:         maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\\n741:         this.sensors.recordRetries(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\\n742:     }\\n743: \\n744:     private void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\\n745:         if (transactionManager != null) {\\n746:             transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\\n747:         }\\n748: \\n749:         if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\\n750:             maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\\n751:         }\\n752:     }\\n753: \\n754:     private void failBatch(ProducerBatch batch,\\n755:                            ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response,\\n756:                            boolean adjustSequenceNumbers) {\\n757:         final RuntimeException topLevelException;\\n758:         if (response.error == Errors.TOPIC_AUTHORIZATION_FAILED)\\n759:             topLevelException = new TopicAuthorizationException(Collections.singleton(batch.topicPartition.topic()));\\n760:         else if (response.error == Errors.CLUSTER_AUTHORIZATION_FAILED)\\n761:             topLevelException = new ClusterAuthorizationException(\\\"The producer is not authorized to do idempotent sends\\\");\\n762:         else\\n763:             topLevelException = response.error.exception(response.errorMessage);\\n764: \\n765:         if (response.recordErrors == null || response.recordErrors.isEmpty()) {\\n766:             failBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\\n767:         } else {\\n768:             Map<Integer, RuntimeException> recordErrorMap = new HashMap<>(response.recordErrors.size());\\n769:             for (ProduceResponse.RecordError recordError : response.recordErrors) {\\n770:                 // The API leaves us with some awkwardness interpreting the errors in the response.\\n771:                 // We cannot differentiate between different error cases (such as INVALID_TIMESTAMP)\\n772:                 // from the single error code at the partition level, so instead we use INVALID_RECORD\\n773:                 // for all failed records and rely on the message to distinguish the cases.\\n774:                 final String errorMessage;\\n775:                 if (recordError.message != null) {\\n776:                     errorMessage = recordError.message;\\n777:                 } else if (response.errorMessage != null) {\\n778:                     errorMessage = response.errorMessage;\\n779:                 } else {\\n780:                     errorMessage = response.error.message();\\n781:                 }\\n782: \\n783:                 // If the batch contained only a single record error, then we can unambiguously\\n784:                 // use the exception type corresponding to the partition-level error code.\\n785:                 if (response.recordErrors.size() == 1) {\\n786:                     recordErrorMap.put(recordError.batchIndex, response.error.exception(errorMessage));\\n787:                 } else {\\n788:                     recordErrorMap.put(recordError.batchIndex, new InvalidRecordException(errorMessage));\\n789:                 }\\n790:             }\\n791: \\n792:             Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions = batchIndex -> {\\n793:                 RuntimeException exception = recordErrorMap.get(batchIndex);\\n794:                 if (exception != null) {\\n795:                     return exception;\\n796:                 } else {\\n797:                     // If the response contains record errors, then the records which failed validation\\n798:                     // will be present in the response. To avoid confusion for the remaining records, we\\n799:                     // return a generic exception.\\n800:                     return new KafkaException(\\\"Failed to append record because it was part of a batch \\\" +\\n801:                         \\\"which had one more more invalid records\\\");\\n802:                 }\\n803:             };\\n804: \\n805:             failBatch(batch, topLevelException, recordExceptions, adjustSequenceNumbers);\\n806:         }\\n807:     }\\n808: \\n809:     private void failBatch(\\n810:         ProducerBatch batch,\\n811:         RuntimeException topLevelException,\\n812:         boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\\n813:     ) {\\n814:         failBatch(batch, topLevelException, batchIndex -> topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\\n815:     }\\n816: \\n817:     private void failBatch(\\n818:         ProducerBatch batch,\\n819:         RuntimeException topLevelException,\\n820:         Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\\n821:         boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\\n822:     ) {\\n823:         this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\\n824: \\n825:         if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\\n826:             if (transactionManager != null) {\\n827:                 try {\\n828:                     // This call can throw an exception in the rare case that there's an invalid state transition\\n829:                     // attempted. } catch (Exception e) {\\n832:                     log.debug(\\\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\\\", e);\\n833:                 }\\n834:             }\\n835:             maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\\n836:         }\\n837:     }\\n838: \\n839:     /**\\n840:      * We can retry a send if the error is transient and the number of attempts taken is fewer than the maximum allowed.\\n841:      * We can also retry OutOfOrderSequence exceptions for future batches, since if the first batch has failed, the\\n842:      * future batches are certain to fail with an OutOfOrderSequence exception.\\n843:      */\\n844:     private boolean canRetry(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response, long now) {\\n845:         return !batch.hasReachedDeliveryTimeout(accumulator.getDeliveryTimeoutMs(), now) &&\\n846:             batch.attempts() < this.retries &&\\n847:             !batch.isDone() &&\\n848:             (transactionManager == null ?\\n849:                     response.error.exception() instanceof RetriableException :\\n850:                     transactionManager.canRetry(response, batch));\\n851:     }\\n852: \\n853:     /**\\n854:      * Transfer the record batches into a list of produce requests on a per-node basis\\n855:      */\\n856:     private void sendProduceRequests(Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> collated, long now) {\\n857:         for (Map.Entry<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> entry : collated.entrySet())\\n858:             sendProduceRequest(now, entry.getKey(), acks, requestTimeoutMs, entry.getValue());\\n859:     }\\n860: \\n861:     /**\\n862:      * Create a produce request from the given record batches\\n863:      */\\n864:     private void sendProduceRequest(long now, int destination, short acks, int timeout, List<ProducerBatch> batches) {\\n865:         if (batches.isEmpty())\\n866:             return;\\n867: \\n868:         final transactionManager.isTransactional()) {\\n893:             transactionalId = transactionManager.transactionalId();\\n894:             useTransactionV1Version = log.trace(\\\"Sent produce request to {}: {}\\\", nodeId, requestBuilder);\\n916:     }\\n917: \\n918:     private Map<String, Uuid> topicIdsForBatches(List<ProducerBatch> batches) {\\n919:       }\n226:     }\n227: \n228:     private boolean hasPendingTransactionalRequests() {\n229:         return transactionManager != null && transactionManager.hasPendingRequests() &&        log.debug(\"Starting Kafka producer I/O thread.\");\n238: \n239:         // main loop, runs until close is called\n240:         while (running) {\n241:             try {\n242:                 runOnce();\n243:             } catch (Exception e) {\n244:                 log.error(\"Uncaught error in kafka producer I/O thread: \", e);\n245:             }\n246:         }\n247: \n248: in the transaction manager, accumulator or waiting for acknowledgment,\n252:         // wait until these are completed.\n253:         while (!forceClose && ((this.accumulator.hasUndrained() || this.client.inFlightRequestCount() > 0) || hasPendingTransactionalRequests())) {\n254:             try {\n255:                 runOnce();\n256:             } catch (Exception e) {\n257:                 log.error(\"Uncaught error in kafka producer I/O thread: \", e);\n258:             }\n259:         }\n260: \n261:         // Abort the transaction if any commit or abort didn't go through the transaction manager's queue\n262:         while (!forceClose && transactionManager != null && transactionManager.hasOngoingTransaction()) {\n263:             if (!transactionManager.isCompleting()) {\n264:                 log.info(\"Aborting incomplete transaction due to shutdown\");\n265:                 try {\n266:                     // It is possible for the transaction manager to throw errors when aborting. Catch these\n267:                     // so as not to interfere with the rest of the shutdown logic.\n268:                     transactionManager.beginAbort();\n269:                 } catch (Exception e) {\n270:                     log.error(\"Error in kafka producer I/O thread while aborting transaction when during closing: \", e);\n271:                     // Force close in case the transactionManager is in error states.\n272:                     forceClose = true;\n273:                 }\n274:             }\n275:             try {\n276:                 runOnce();\n277:             } catch (Exception e) {\n278:                 log.error(\"Uncaught error in kafka producer I/O thread: \", e);\n279:             }\n280:         }\n281: \n282:         if (forceClose) {\n283:             // We need to fail all the incomplete transactional requests and batches and wake up the threads waiting on\n284:             // the futures.\n285:             if (transactionManager != null) {\n286:                 log.debug(\"Aborting incomplete transactional requests due to forced shutdown\");\n287:                 transactionManager.close();\n288:             }\n289: this.client.close();\n294:         } catch (Exception e) {\n295:             log.error(\"Failed to close network client\", e);\n296:         }\n297: \n298:         log.debug(\"Shutdown of Kafka producer I/O thread has completed.\");\n299:     }\n300: \n301:     /**\n302:      * Run a single iteration of sending\n303:      *\n304:      */\n305:     void runOnce() {\n306:         if (transactionManager != null) {\n307:             try {\n308:                 transactionManager.maybeResolveSequences();\n309: \n310:                 RuntimeException lastError = transactionManager.lastError();\n311: \n312:                 // do not continue sending if the transaction manager is in a failed state\n313:                 if (transactionManager.hasFatalError()) {\n314:                     if (lastError != null)\n315:                         maybeAbortBatches(lastError);\n316:                     client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\n317:                     return;\n318:                 }\n319: \n320:                 if (transactionManager.hasAbortableError() && shouldHandleAuthorizationError(lastError)) {\n321:                     return;\n322:                 }\n323: \n324:                 // Check whether we need a new producerId. If so, we will enqueue an InitProducerId\n325:                 // request which will be sent below\n326:                 transactionManager.bumpIdempotentEpochAndResetIdIfNeeded();\n327: \n328:                 if (maybeSendAndPollTransactionalRequest()) {\n329:                     return;\n330:                 }\n331:             } catch (AuthenticationException e) {\n332:                 // This is already logged as error, but propagated here to perform any clean ups.\n333:                 log.trace(\"Authentication exception while processing transactional request\", e);\n334:                 transactionManager.authenticationFailed(e);\n335:             }\n336:         }\n337: \n338:         long currentTimeMs = time.milliseconds();\n339:         long pollTimeout = sendProducerData(currentTimeMs);\n340:         client.poll(pollTimeout, currentTimeMs);\n341:     }\n342: \n343:     // We handle {@code TransactionalIdAuthorizationException} and {@code ClusterAuthorizationException} by first\n344:     // failing the inflight requests, then transition the state to UNINITIALIZED so that the user doesn't need to\n345:     // instantiate the producer again.\n346:     private boolean shouldHandleAuthorizationError(RuntimeException exception) {\n347:         if (exception instanceof TransactionalIdAuthorizationException ||\n348:                         exception instanceof ClusterAuthorizationException) {\n349:             transactionManager.failPendingRequests(new AuthenticationException(exception));\n350:             maybeAbortBatches(exception);\n351:             transactionManager.transitionToUninitialized(exception);\n352:             return true;\n353:         }\n354:         return false;\n355:     }\n356: \n357:     private long sendProducerData(long now) {\n358:         MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot = metadata.fetchMetadataSnapshot();\n359:         // get the list of partitions with data ready to send\n360:         RecordAccumulator.ReadyCheckResult result = this.accumulator.ready(metadataSnapshot, now);\n361: \n362:         // if there are any partitions whose leaders are not known yet, force metadata update\n363:         if (!result.unknownLeaderTopics.isEmpty()) {\n364:             // The set of topics with unknown leader contains topics with leader election pending as well as\n365:             // topics which may have expired. Add the topic again to metadata to ensure it is included\n366:             // and request metadata update, since there are messages to send to the topic.\n367:             for (String topic : result.unknownLeaderTopics)\n368:                 this.metadata.add(topic, now);\n369: \n370:             log.debug(\"Requesting metadata update due to unknown leader topics from the batched records: {}\",\n371:                 result.unknownLeaderTopics);\n372:             this.metadata.requestUpdate(false);\n373:         }\n374: \n375:         // remove any nodes we aren't ready to send to\n376:         Iterator<Node> iter = result.readyNodes.iterator();\n377:         long notReadyTimeout = Long.MAX_VALUE;\n378:         while (iter.hasNext()) {\n379:             Node node = iter.next();\n380:             if (!this.client.ready(node, now)) {\n381:                 // Update just the readyTimeMs of the latency stats, so that it moves forward\n382:                 // every time the batch is ready (then the difference between readyTimeMs and\n383:                 // drainTimeMs would represent how long data is waiting for the node).\n384:                 this.accumulator.updateNodeLatencyStats(node.id(), now, false);\n385:                 iter.remove();\n386:                 notReadyTimeout = Math.min(notReadyTimeout, this.client.pollDelayMs(node, now));\n387:             } else {\n388:                 // Update both readyTimeMs and drainTimeMs, this would \"reset\" the node\n389:                 // latency.\n390:                 this.accumulator.updateNodeLatencyStats(node.id(), now, true);\n391:             }\n392:         }\n393: \n394:         // create produce requests\n395:         Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(metadataSnapshot, result.readyNodes, this.maxRequestSize, now);\n396:         addToInflightBatches(batches);\n397:         if (guaranteeMessageOrder) {\n398:             // Mute all the partitions drained\n399:             for (List<ProducerBatch> batchList : batches.values()) {\n400:                 for (ProducerBatch batch : batchList)\n401:                     this.accumulator.mutePartition(batch.topicPartition);\n402:             }\n403:         }\n404: \n405:         accumulator.resetNextBatchExpiryTime();\n406:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n407:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\n408:         expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n409: \n410:         // Reset the producer id if an expired batch has previously been sent to the broker. Also update the metrics\n411:         // for expired batches. see the documentation of @TransactionState.resetIdempotentProducerId to understand why\n412:         // we need to reset the producer id here.\n413:         if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty())\n414:             log.trace(\"Expired {} batches in accumulator\", expiredBatches.size());\n415:         for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n416:             String errorMessage = \"Expiring \" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \" record(s) for \" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n417:                 + \":\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \" ms has passed since batch creation\";\n418:             failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\n419:             if (transactionManager != null && expiredBatch.inRetry()) {\n420:                 // This ensures that no new batches are drained until the current in flight batches are fully resolved.\n421:                 transactionManager.markSequenceUnresolved(expiredBatch);\n422:             }\n423:         }\n424:         sensors.updateProduceRequestMetrics(batches);\n425: \n426:         // If we have any nodes that are ready to send + have sendable data, poll with 0 timeout so this can immediately\n427:         // loop and try sending more data. Otherwise, the timeout will be the smaller value between next batch expiry\n428:         // time, and the delay time for checking data availability. Note that the nodes may have data that isn't yet\n429:         // sendable due to lingering, backing off, etc. This specifically does not include nodes with sendable data\n430:         // that aren't ready to send since they would cause busy looping.\n431:         long pollTimeout = Math.min(result.nextReadyCheckDelayMs, notReadyTimeout);\n432:         pollTimeout = Math.min(pollTimeout, this.accumulator.nextExpiryTimeMs() - now);\n433:         pollTimeout = Math.max(pollTimeout, 0);\n434:         if (!result.readyNodes.isEmpty()) {\n435:             log.trace(\"Nodes with data ready to send: {}\", result.readyNodes);\n436:             // if some partitions are already ready to be sent, the select time would be 0;\n437:             // otherwise if some partition already has some data accumulated but not ready yet,\n438:             // the select time will be the time difference between now and its linger expiry time;\n439:             // otherwise the select time will be the time difference between now and the metadata expiry time;\n440:             pollTimeout = 0;\n441:         }\n442:         sendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n443:         return pollTimeout;\n444:     }\n445: \n446:     /**\n447:      * Returns true if a transactional request is sent or polled, or if a FindCoordinator request is enqueued\n448:      */\n449:     private boolean maybeSendAndPollTransactionalRequest() {\n450:         if (transactionManager.hasInFlightRequest()) {\n451:             // as long as there are outstanding transactional requests, we simply wait for them to return\n452:             client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\n453:             return true;\n454:         }\n455: \n456:         if (transactionManager.hasAbortableError()) {\n457:             accumulator.abortUndrainedBatches(transactionManager.lastError());\n458:         } else if (transactionManager.isAborting()) {\n459:             accumulator.abortUndrainedBatches(new TransactionAbortedException());\n460:         }\n461: \n462:         TransactionManager.TxnRequestHandler nextRequestHandler = transactionManager.nextRequest(accumulator.hasIncomplete());\n463:         if (nextRequestHandler == null)\n464:             return false;\n465: \n466:         AbstractRequest.Builder<?> requestBuilder = nextRequestHandler.requestBuilder();\n467:         Node targetNode = null;\n468:         try {\n469:             FindCoordinatorRequest.CoordinatorType coordinatorType = nextRequestHandler.coordinatorType();\n470:             targetNode = coordinatorType != null ?\n471:                     transactionManager.coordinator(coordinatorType) :\n472:                     client.leastLoadedNode(time.milliseconds()).node();\n473:             if (targetNode != null) {\n474:                 if (!awaitNodeReady(targetNode, coordinatorType)) {\n475:                     log.trace(\"Target node {} not ready within request timeout, will retry when node is ready.\", targetNode);\n476:                     maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(nextRequestHandler);\n477:                     return true;\n478:                 }\n479:             } else if (coordinatorType != null) {\n480:                 log.trace(\"Coordinator not known for {}, will retry {} after finding coordinator.\", coordinatorType, requestBuilder.apiKey());\n481:                 maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(nextRequestHandler);\n482:                 return true;\n483:             } else {\n484:                 log.trace(\"No nodes available to send requests, will poll and retry when until a node is ready.\");\n485:                 transactionManager.retry(nextRequestHandler);\n486:                 client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\n487:                 return true;\n488:             }\n489: \n490:             if (nextRequestHandler.isRetry())\n491:                 time.sleep(nextRequestHandler.retryBackoffMs());\n492: \n493:             long currentTimeMs = time.milliseconds();\n494:             ClientRequest clientRequest = client.newClientRequest(targetNode.idString(), requestBuilder, currentTimeMs,\n495:                 true, requestTimeoutMs, nextRequestHandler);\n496:             log.debug(\"Sending transactional request {} to node {} with correlation ID {}\", requestBuilder, targetNode, clientRequest.correlationId());\n497:             client.send(clientRequest, currentTimeMs);\n498:             transactionManager.setInFlightCorrelationId(clientRequest.correlationId());\n499:             client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\n500:             return true;\n501:         } catch (IOException e) {\n502:             log.debug(\"Disconnect from {} while trying to send request {}. Going \" +\n503:                     \"to back off and retry.\", targetNode, requestBuilder, e);\n504:             // We break here so that we pick up the FindCoordinator request immediately.\n505:             maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(nextRequestHandler);\n506:             return true;\n507:         }\n508:     }\n509: \n510:     private void maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(TransactionManager.TxnRequestHandler nextRequestHandler) {\n511:         if (nextRequestHandler.needsCoordinator()) {\n512:             transactionManager.lookupCoordinator(nextRequestHandler);\n513:         } else {\n514:             // For non-coordinator requests, sleep here to prevent a tight loop when no node is available\n515:             time.sleep(retryBackoffMs);\n516:             metadata.requestUpdate(false);\n517:         }\n518: \n519:         transactionManager.retry(nextRequestHandler);\n520:     }\n521: \n522:     private void maybeAbortBatches(RuntimeException exception) {\n523:         if (accumulator.hasIncomplete()) {\n524:             log.error(\"Aborting producer batches due to fatal error\", exception);\n525:             accumulator.abortBatches(exception);\n526:         }\n527:     }\n528: \n529:     /**\n530:      * Start closing the sender (won't actually complete until all data is sent out)\n531:      */\n532:     public void initiateClose() {\n533:         // Ensure accumulator is closed first to guarantee that no more appends are accepted after\n534:         // breaking from the sender loop. Otherwise, we may miss some callbacks when shutting down.\n535:         this.accumulator.close();\n536:         this.running = false;\n537:         this.wakeup();\n538:     }\n539: \n540:     /**\n541:      * Closes the sender without sending out any pending messages.\n542:      */\n543:     public void forceClose() {\n544:         this.forceClose = true;\n545:         initiateClose();\n546:     }\n547: \n548:     public boolean isRunning() {\n549:         return running;\n550:     }\n551: \n552:     private boolean awaitNodeReady(Node node, FindCoordinatorRequest.CoordinatorType coordinatorType) throws IOException {\n553:         if (NetworkClientUtils.awaitReady(client, node, time, requestTimeoutMs)) {\n554:             if (coordinatorType == FindCoordinatorRequest.CoordinatorType.TRANSACTION) {\n555:                 // Indicate to the transaction manager that the coordinator is ready, allowing it to check ApiVersions\n556:                 // This allows us to bump transactional epochs even if the coordinator is temporarily unavailable at\n557:                 // the time when the abortable error is /**\n566:      * Handle a produce response\n567:      */\n568:     private void handleProduceResponse(ClientResponse response, Map<TopicPartition, ProducerBatch> batches, Map<Uuid, String> topicNames, long now) {\n569:         RequestHeader requestHeader = response.requestHeader();\n570:         int correlationId = requestHeader.correlationId();\n571:         if (response.wasTimedOut()) {\n572:             log.trace(\"Cancelled request with header {} due to the last request to node {} timed out\",\n573:                 requestHeader, response.destination());\n574:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\n575:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.REQUEST_TIMED_OUT, String.format(\"Disconnected from node %s due to timeout\", response.destination())),\n576:                         correlationId, now, null);\n577:         } else if (response.wasDisconnected()) {\n578:             log.trace(\"Cancelled request with header {} due to node {} being disconnected\",\n579:                 requestHeader, response.destination());\n580:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\n581:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.NETWORK_EXCEPTION, String.format(\"Disconnected from node %s\", response.destination())),\n582:                         correlationId, now, null);\n583:         } else if (response.versionMismatch() != null) {\n584:             log.warn(\"Cancelled request {} due to a version mismatch with node {}\",\n585:                     response, response.destination(), response.versionMismatch());\n586:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\n587:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.UNSUPPORTED_VERSION), correlationId, now, null);\n588:         } else {\n589:             log.trace(\"Received produce response from node {} with correlation id {}\", response.destination(), correlationId);\n590:             // if we have a response, parse it\n591:             if (response.hasResponse()) {\n592:                 // Sender should exercise PartitionProduceResponse rather than ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse\n593:                 // https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-10696\n594:                 ProduceResponse produceResponse = (ProduceResponse) response.responseBody();\n595:                 // This will be set by completeBatch.\n596:                 Map<TopicPartition, Metadata.LeaderIdAndEpoch> partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo = new HashMap<>();\n597:                 produceResponse.data().responses().forEach(r -> r.partitionResponses().forEach(p -> {\n598:                     ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse partResp = new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(\n599:                             Errors.forCode(p.errorCode()),\n600:                             p.baseOffset(),\n601:                             p.logAppendTimeMs(),\n602:                             p.logStartOffset(),\n603:                             p.recordErrors()\n604:                                 .stream()\n605:                                 .map(e -> new ProduceResponse.RecordError(e.batchIndex(), e.batchIndexErrorMessage()))\n606:                                 .collect(Collectors.toList()),\n607:                             p.errorMessage(),\n608:                             p.currentLeader());\n609: \n610:                     // Version 13 drop topic name and add support to topic id.\n611:                     // We need to find batch based on topic id and partition index only as\n612:                     // topic name in the response will be empty.\n613:                     // For older versions, topic id is zero, and we will find the batch based on the topic name.\n614:                     TopicPartition tp =        new TopicPartition(r.name(), p.index());\n617: \n618:                     ProducerBatch batch = batches.get(tp);\n619:                     if (batch == null) {\n620:                         throw new IllegalStateException(\"Can't find batch created for topic id \" + r.topicId() +\n621:                                 \" topic name \" + r.name() + \" partition \" + p.index() + \" using \" + topicNames);\n622:                     }\n623:                     completeBatch(batch, partResp, correlationId, now, partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo);\n624:                 }));\n625: \n626: In sendProducerData() at line 395 of Sender.java:\n   - Batches are drained from the accumulator\n\n2. At line 406-408:\n   - Expired inflight batches are identified\n   - Expired batches from accumulator are identified\n\n3. At line 418:\n   - failBatch is called for expired batches\n   - This calls maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch() (line 835 of failBatch)\n   - Which calls accumulator.deallocate() (line 1032 of RecordAccumulator)\n   - Which calls free.deallocate() (the BufferPool)\n\n4. At line 442:\n   - sendProduceRequests is called to send the batches that were drained at line 395\n\nThe race condition is:\n- An expired batch is identified at line 406-408\n- Its buffer is deallocated back to the BufferPool at line 418\n- But if this batch was in the inflight batches (those that were already drained and are being sent), the buffer is still referenced by the network request that's being written\n- The deallocated buffer can be immediately reused by another batch (since we're on the sender thread)\n- This means the memory being written to the network is now being used by another batch\n\nWait, let me re-read the code more carefully. Looking at line 395:\n```java\nMap<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(metadataSnapshot, result.readyNodes, this.maxRequestSize, now);\n```\n\nThis drains new batches. Then at line 406-408:\n\n\n```java\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\nexpiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n```\n\nThe code collects both expired inflight batches (already sent) and expired batches still in the accumulator. When failBatch is called on these expired batches, it deallocates their buffers immediately. The problem is that inflight batches may still have their buffers referenced by in-flight network requests, so deallocating them creates a use-after-free scenario where the buffer gets reused by another batch while the network layer is still writing the original data. The batch's buffer is still being written to the network by a previous call, so I need to examine how ProducerBatch manages the buffer lifecycle. Looking at the batch object, it holds a reference to the underlying buffer that gets serialized and sent over the network. Now I see it. The getExpiredInflightBatches method gets batches that have reached the delivery timeout from the inFlightBatches. These are batches that have been drained and a request has been sent (line 396: they are added to inFlightBatches).\n\nSo the race condition is:1. At line 395, batches are drained from the accumulator\n2. At line 396, addToInflightBatches is called to add them to the inFlightBatches map\n3. At line 442, sendProduceRequests is called to send the batches4. Later, at line 406, getExpiredInflightBatches is called to get expired inflight batches5. If a batch has expired, it's added to the expiredBatches list\n6. At line 418, failBatch is called for the expired batch\n7. At line 835 (in failBatch), maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch is called\n8. At line 174 (in maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch), accumulator.deallocate is called\n9. At line 1032 (in RecordAccumulator.deallocate), free.deallocate is called\n\nNow the issue is that when the batch expires:- The request might still be in the KafkaClient's send queue or being written to the network\n- The buffer is returned to the BufferPool and can be immediately reused by another batch\n- But the request is still being written with the original buffer reference\n\nHowever, I need to think about whether this causes the \"wrong topic\" issue. The topic name is not in the buffer, it's part of the batch's topicPartition field. So how would the buffer reuse cause a message to appear on the wrong topic?\n\nLet me think about the flow again:1. A batch for topic A is created with buffer X\n2. The batch's records (from buffer X) are added to the produce request\n\n\n3. The batch is drained and added to inFlightBatches\n4. sendProduceRequests is called to send the request\n5. The client.send(clientRequest) is called, which queues the request to be sent\n6. Later, the batch expires\n7. The batch is deallocated, and buffer X is returned to the pool\n8. A new batch for topic B is created with buffer X (reused)\n9. The produce request for topic A is being written to the network with buffer X, but buffer X now contains data for topic B\n\nWait, but the buffer contains the actual record data (key/value), not the topic name. The topic name is in the ProduceRequest itself, which is separate from the buffer. So reusing the buffer shouldn't change which topic the message goes to.\n\nLooking at sendProduceRequest, the ProduceRequestData is constructed with TopicProduceData objects that reference the MemoryRecords from each batch. The topic information comes from the batch's TopicPartition, not from the buffer itself. So even if the buffer is reused, the ProduceRequestData still points to the correct topic because it was already serialized with the right metadata. The topicNames map is passed to the RequestCompletionHandler callback, which uses it when handling the produce response. However, the core issue isn't about the request header itself being incorrect—it's about how the batch lifecycle interacts with serialization timing. Now I see the full race condition:\n\n1. In sendProduceRequest:\n   - ProduceRequest.Builder is created with MemoryRecords from the batch\n   - ClientRequest is created with the builder\n   - client.send(clientRequest, now) is called (this just enqueues it)\n\n2. The enqueued ClientRequest is later processed when poll() is called:\n   - doSend() is called with the ClientRequest\n   - At line 608, request.toSend(header) is called, which builds the Send object\n   - The Send object holds a reference to the MemoryRecords' buffer\n   - The Send is added to the selector to be sent to the network\n\n3. But if a batch expires before line 608 is executed:\n   - failBatch is called\n   - maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch is called\n   - The batch's buffer is deallocated and returned to the pool\n   - The buffer can be immediately reused by another batch\n   - When line 608 is finally executed, the Send object gets the buffer reference, but it's already been reused\n\n4. When the Send is written to the network:\n   - The buffer content has been overwritten by the new batch\n   - So the original request contains data from the wrong batch\n\nThis could definitely cause messages to appear on the wrong topic! Here's the scenario:\n- Batch for topic A is created with buffer X, records for topic A are written to buffer X\n- The batch is drained and added to inFlightBatches\n- sendProduceRequests is called, which calls client.send() to enqueue the request\n- Before the enqueued request is processed (in the next poll() cycle), the batch expires\n- failBatch is called, and buffer X is deallocated and returned to the pool\n- A new batch for topic B is created with buffer X (reused from pool)\n- Records for topic B are written to buffer X\n- The Send object for topic A is finally built and gets buffer X\n\n\n- But buffer X now contains records for topic B, so the request is sent with topic A header but topic B data!\n\nThe core problem is that buffers get deallocated while requests referencing them are still in flight through the network layer. I need to find where to prevent this. Several potential solutions come to mind: keeping buffers allocated until responses arrive, preventing deallocation while requests are pending, copying buffer contents before deallocation, or blocking batch expiration once a batch has been drained.\n\nThe most promising approach seems to be preventing deallocation of batches that have already been sent to the network but haven't yet received their responses. If the batch expires in sendProducerData (lines 406-423), the buffer is deallocated. But then in client.poll() (line 340), the Send object is built and tries to get the deallocated buffer.\n\nActually, wait. Let me check if there's a time gap between sendProducerData and client.poll(). They're called one after the other in the same run() iteration, so the time shouldn't change much.\n\nLet me re-read the getExpiredInflightBatches logic. It checks if `batch.hasReachedDeliveryTimeout()`. So it's checking if the batch has reached the delivery timeout (linger.ms + request.timeout.ms).\n\nThe race condition would happen if:1. A batch is drained and added to inFlightBatches at the SAME time it reaches the delivery timeout\n2. sendProducerData continues and calls getExpiredInflightBatches, which returns this batch\n3. failBatch is called, deallocating the buffer\n4. So there's a window where the batch is in-flight but the request hasn't been processed yet, and during that window it could expire and get failed while the request is still queued. enqueued immediately in sendProduceRequests, so it should be processed in the next poll() call.\n\nLooking at the actual bug description more carefully: \"when an in-flight `ProducerBatch` expires or its broker disconnects, the batch's pooled `ByteBuffer` is returned to the `BufferPool` and immediately reused by a new batch — while the original batch's request is still being written to the network by the `Sender` thread.\"\n\nThe core issue is that the Send object is being written asynchronously to the network. In NetworkClient.doSend(), the Send gets added to the selector via `selector.send(new NetworkSend(clientRequest.destination(), send))`, meaning the buffer deallocation happens while the write is still in progress.\n\nThe Send holds references to the batch's buffers through the SendBuilder's buffers list. When the buffer is deallocated and reused by another batch, the Send ends up writing the reused buffer's content instead of the original data. The fix needs to prevent buffer deallocation until the Send completes writing to the network.\n\nInflight batches shouldn't be deallocated immediately upon expiration—they should only be freed once the response arrives or the request times out. The failBatch method gets called when responses are received with errors or when batches expire, but deallocating an inflight batch risks freeing its buffer while the network write is still in progress. A safer approach would be to defer deallocation for inflight batches until the response is actually received. The completeBatch method also triggers deallocation, so any fix needs to account for all deallocation {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01VEvP5E4T5cu3eMgA1vZXN1","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01VoQqNSX6QZ12S7JCuW8e99","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"## Files Examined\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java — entry point for tracing bug, contains sendProducerData() and failBatch() methods\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java — manages batch lifecycle and buffer allocation/deallocation\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java — pooled ByteBuffer management\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/NetworkClient.java — network request handling, where Send is actually built\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java — builds Send objects with zero-copy buffer references\n\n## Dependency Chain\n1. **Symptom observed in**: Users report messages from topic A appearing on topic B (rare, bursts during network disruption)\n2. **Called from**: Sender.java `sendProducerData()` (line 357-443)\n3. **Critical section 1**: Lines 395-396 - Batches are drained from accumulator and added to inflight batches\n4. **Critical section 2**: Lines 406-408 - Expired inflight batches are identified\n5. **Critical section 3**: Lines 418-422 - `failBatch()` is called for expired batches, triggering deallocation\n6. **Bug triggered by**: RecordAccumulator.java `deallocate()` (line 1027-1033) and BufferPool.java `deallocate()` (line 260-275)\n7. **Race occurs during**: NetworkClient.java `doSend()` (line 601-618), specifically at line 608 where `request.toSend()` is called\n8. **Buffer reuse happens in**: BufferPool.java `allocate()` (line 107-175), at lines 124-125 where free buffers are immediately reused\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### File: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n### Function: sendProducerData() and failBatch()\n### Lines: ~418 (in sendProducerData) → ~835 (in failBatch) → line 174 (in maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch)\n\n### Explanation\n\n**The Bug:**\nWhen an in-flight `ProducerBatch` (one that has been sent to the network but hasn't received a response) expires due to delivery timeout, the batch's pooled `ByteBuffer` is immediately deallocated and returned to the `BufferPool`. The deallocation happens BEFORE the network Send object is fully constructed and transmitted. This creates a race condition where:\n\n1. At line 395-396 of `sendProducerData()`: A batch is drained from the accumulator and immediately added to `inFlightBatches`\n2. At line 442: `sendProduceRequests()` enqueues the request with the batch's `MemoryRecords`\n3. Between sendProducerData() return and the NEXT client.poll() call: The batch is checked for expiration\n4. At line 406: `getExpiredInflightBatches()` returns batches that have exceeded delivery timeout\n5. At line 418: `failBatch()` is called for the expired batch\n6. In `failBatch()` at line 835: `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called\n7. In `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 174: `accumulator.deallocate(batch)` is called\n8. In `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` at line 1032: `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), ...)` returns the buffer to `BufferPool`\n9. At `BufferPool.deallocate()` line 264-265: The buffer is cleared and added back to the free list\n10. **Critical Race**: Before the client.poll() call completes, when `NetworkClient.doSend()` finally processes the queued request:\n    - At line 608: `request.toSend(header)` is called\n    - This calls `SendBuilder.buildRequestSend()` → `buildSend()` (line 208-225)\n    - At line 223: `apiMessage.write()` serializes the ProduceRequestData\n    - This eventually calls `SendBuilder.writeRecords()` (line 137-148)\n    - At line 140: `addBuffer(((MemoryRecords) records).buffer())` gets the batch's buffer reference\n    - **BUT** the buffer has already been deallocated and reused by a NEW batch for a different topic!\n\n11. **The Corruption**: The Send object now contains a reference to a buffer that:\n    - Was originally allocated for batch A on topic X\n    - Has been deallocated and is now being used by batch B on topic Y\n    - Contains data for topic Y instead of topic X\n    - The request header still says \"topic X\", but the record data is from \"topic Y\"\n\n12. When the Send is written to the network, the broker receives a Produce request with:\n    - Header: Topic X, Partition N\n    - Records: Data from Topic Y\n    - Result: Messages intended for topic X are persisted to topic Y\n\n### Why Topic Name Is Corrupted (Not Just Data)\n\nThe critical issue is in `SendBuilder.writeRecords()`. It stores a **reference** to the buffer, not a copy. When `ProduceRequestData` is serialized during `buildSend()`, the `MemoryRecords.buffer()` is accessed at line 140. If the buffer has been reused, it contains different data AND possibly has been reset to position 0 with new record content, so even the record structure itself may have changed.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to **prevent deallocating in-flight batches that are still pending transmission**. There are two approaches:\n\n### Approach 1: Don't deallocate pending inflight batches when they expire (RECOMMENDED)\n\nIn `Sender.failBatch()`, check if the batch has a pending request in the network layer. If so, don't deallocate it immediately - let the response handler deallocate it instead.\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(\n    ProducerBatch batch,\n    RuntimeException topLevelException,\n    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n) {\n    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                // This call can throw an exception in the rare case that there's an invalid state transition\n                // attempted. Catch these so as not to interfere with the rest of the logic.\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\\\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\\\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // Don't deallocate inflight batches immediately - their buffer may still be referenced by\n+       // a Send object that hasn't been fully transmitted. Wait for the response handler to deallocate.\n+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Approach 2: Don't expire inflight batches in sendProducerData() - let them timeout at the request level\n\nIn `sendProducerData()`, skip expiring batches that are in the inflight set. They will eventually timeout at the request timeout level and be cleaned up by `handleProduceResponse()` with appropriate errors.\n\n```diff\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\nexpiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n\n// Reset the producer id if an expired batch has previously been sent to the broker. Also update the metrics\n// for expired batches. see the documentation of @TransactionState.resetIdempotentProducerId to understand why\n// we need to reset the producer id here.\nif (!expiredBatches.isEmpty())\n    log.trace(\\\"Expired {} batches in accumulator\\\", expiredBatches.size());\nfor (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n+   // Don't fail/deallocate inflight batches - they will be cleaned up when their response arrives\n+   // or when the request times out in NetworkClient\n+   if (inFlightBatches.containsValue(expiredBatch))\n+       continue;\n+\n    String errorMessage = \\\"Expiring \\\" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \\\" record(s) for \\\" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n        + \\\":\\\" + (now -
